PT J
AU Biebeler, H
AF Biebeler, H
TI Social norms as an independent concept for explaining behaviour
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The paper aims to show how social norms influence conservationist behaviour. One approach to this problem, taking norms as basic and irreducible, holds that norms are based on values and not on the anticipated reactions of the social environment to certain behaviour. According to this view, norms are to be understood as a form of judging behaviour, characteristics and beliefs, which is backed by the granting or withdrawal of esteem. Conceptualized like this, norms have powers of their own. In contrast to this, rational choice theory regards norms as nothing but requests from the mighty, implying that the existence of norms depends on constellations of individual wishes and power. It is doubtful whether these constellations are stable enough to guarantee morally acceptable behaviour and the persistence of social order. Following the value-based approach, the paper presents a scheme encompassing moral norms, norms of proper conduct and norms of impression, the latter being divided into situation-related norms, norms of reason and image norms. A behavioural model is developed combining these normative perspectives and non-normative personal dispositions, which is then applied to two examples of environmental behaviour and tested empirically.
C1 Univ Cologne, Inst Angew Sozialforsch, D-50939 Cologne, Germany.
RP Biebeler, H (corresponding author), Univ Cologne, Inst Angew Sozialforsch, Greinstr 2, D-50939 Cologne, Germany.

TI Conflicts over memory and their "hedging"
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The aim of the article is to provide heuristic categories for the description of contemporary conflicts over collective memory in order to specify their development and the framing conditions of their civil and cooperative settling. I distinguish between two ideal types of memory conflicts: on the one hand, conflicts of interest, in which collective memories serve as vehicles for the demonstration and promotion of particular interests, and, on the other hand, cultural conflicts, in which opposing positions quarrel over the definition of an imagined community. With the help of this heuristic construction it can be demonstrated that civil and cooperative conflict settlement is not possible unless the parties involved in the conflict refrain from treating it as a manifestation of one and only one of the ideal types, Memory conflicts may escalate if either side tries to do so. In such cases of de-differentiated conflicts the basic mechanisms of civil settlement of conflicts of interest as well as of cultural conflicts are delegitimated. The main thesis is illustrated by an analysis of the contemporary debate over Stalinism in Russia.

AU Birkelbach, K
AF Birkelbach, K
TI Religious beliefs between youth and midlife
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The paper presents results of a study analysing the development of religious beliefs of young adults. In a first step, the development of religious attitudes of former grammar school students (n = 1596) between the ages of 30 and 43 ( 1984 and 1997), as indicated in six statements on the spiritual meaning of life, is examined and compared to the development in several age-cohorts from a cross-section of the West German population between 1982 and 1992. Results show a significant change in religious beliefs for both the cross-section sample and the sample of educationally privileged grammar school students. The belief in a personal god giving meaning to one's life becomes less important while more abstract beliefs, such as the belief in life after death, gain importance. This result points to a trend towards emancipation from a dogmatic, church-dominated understanding of religion, but not to an end of religiousness as such. In a second step, it is examined whether the development within the sample of grammar school students, which is particularly clear for the younger cohorts, is due not only to general period effects, but also to experiences in the course of one's individual lift: between the ages of 30 and 43. It can be shown that, although religious socialisation still influences religious attitudes at the age of 43, biographical circumstances also have an impact on religious attitudes.

AU Dubiel, H
AF Dubiel, H
TI Uncivil societies
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Many social and political scientists suspect the concept of 'civil society' of being a 'fair weather'-theory, insensitive towards 'uncivil' phenomena like domination, violence and inequality. The initial argument of the article is that, contrary to this prejudice, it has always been the experience of domination, violence and inequality which has triggered the debates on that concept. The use of the term 'civil society' has always been guided by an interest in the borderline on which an ever precarious normalcy may tip into barbarity. This holds for phenomena as varied as the re-introduction of the term by East European liberation movements, its adoption by the New Social Movements of the eighties, its use with regard to so called 'disaffected democracies' and new forms of barbarity in the nineties, and its present use in criticizing a 'predatory globalization'. The term 'uncivil' originated in Shakespeare's England and refers to symptoms of discord, distrust, fear, arbitrary use of violence and political oppression-symptoms which occur when a social or moral order is about to collapse.

TI The erosion of skilled labour? Questions and objections regarding a
   German debate.
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The thesis that the German dual system of vocational training as well as skilled tabour in general are threatened by erosion is challenged in this article by theoretical arguments and empirical evidence from Norwegian studies. The question is discussed whether the 'erosion thesis' exaggerates the discontinuity of industrial organization principles, thus prematurely devaluating the productive potentials of skilled workers. The author points out that the presumption of an erosion process is based on a restricted concept of 'Beruf' (vocation) and of work organization. Rather than seeing 'process orientation' as an organizational principle that contradicts the concept of 'Beruf, the author argues that it could supplement professional responsibilities, thus extending and renewing the concept. He wonders whether the 'erosion thesis' sufficiently considers the criticism of the neo-classical view of economic behaviour, which was brought forward during the eighties. According to this criticism, the socialization and integration of skilled workers into a professional community can be seen as the well-working institutionalization of a 'practical professionalism' which also includes innovative and future-oriented capacities. Finally, a research perspective is sketched out regarding the future of vocational training and skilled tabour.

AU Lindemann, G
AF Lindemann, G
TI The reflexive anthropology of the process of civilization
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Drawing upon the theory of reflexive anthropology the article offers a new perspective on Elias' theory of the process of civilization. The basic assumption of reflexive anthropology is that the range of social actors cannot be restricted to living human beings but may include other entities as well. Among other things, this approach allows to understand the emergence and further development of the criminal prosecution and the capital punishment of animals. The prosecution of animals was a wide-spread phenomenon in Europe from the end of the 13th century until the late 17th century. During that period, animals were treated as persons or subjects with a free will, who were responsible for their deeds. In early medieval society, however, the notion of individual guilt and responsibility had not existed in secular contexts. The prerequisite for the development of the notion of individual guilt was a change in legal practices, which took place in the 12th century. At that time trials were rationalized (Max Weber), i.e., judges referred to a body of written law which was regarded as man-made and alterable, and trials were held with the aim of finding out what had actually happened and who was responsible, That process of rationalization was the precondition for the inclusion of animals into legal procedures. The article examines in depth the conditions which allowed animals to become responsible subjects of criminal law for almost 400 years. Furthermore. it depicts the emergence of the strict separation between the realms of nature, culture, and the supernatural, which was first conceived in the 17th and 18th centuries and which constitutes a central feature of the civilised world we live in today.

TI The paradoxes of knowledge transfer. Pragmatic interpenetration and
   border maintenance: The 'new liaison' between social sciences and
   practical fields
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Social sciences have recently encountered both enthusiastic celebrations of their own efficiency and increasing demands for their practical efficacy. On the one hand, it has become obvious that social research hardly influences social practices directly and on the intended paths of implementation, but usually indirectly and by the rather uncontrollable diffusion of concepts and perspectives. Nevertheless, there have been increasing claims by representatives of economy and politics to an enhanced practical consulting competence on the part of social sciences. Drawing on the results of an empirical study on the practical relevance of social sciences, the article analyses that claim as a paradoxical one which tends to underestimate the functional need for scientific autonomy. It proposes a model for the pragmatic transfer of knowledge based on the symmetrical autonomy of both practical and scientific fields, on individual translation skills, and on the institutional provision of 'realms of translation'. Contrary to what is often maintained: that social sciences should turn into a service organisation, the improvement of knowledge transfer rather calls for a context-specific pragmatic opening of a still autonomous scientific system.

TI The fiction of the natural body. Doping in the second age of modernity
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The number of professional athletes being caught at drug abuse ("doping") has been rising continuously during the past years. The revelation of and public attention for the wide-spread use of performance-enhancing drugs among athletes questions the legitimacy of professional sports. What is at stake is its reputation in society and its professional ethics. Although the responsible organizations and persons have recognized the urgency of the problem, they have up to now failed to solve it. The reason for this crisis-so the author claims-lies in the fact that the organizations and institutions of professional sports cling, against much evidence, to a clear distinction between the 'natural' (i.e. non-manipulated) body and the manipulated, doped body, It is this fiction of a 'natural body' that prevents institutional learning and thus blocks a solution to the doping crisis. This argument is developed with reference to contemporary theories of modernity set forth by Ulrich Beck and Bruno Latour, Its conclusion is that the institutional crisis in professional sports will not be brought to an end unless the fiction of the natural body is dropped.

TI The concept of "lifestyle" in social structure research - A critical
   appraisal
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID SOCIETY
AB During the past 15 years the concept of "lifestyle" has increasingly been used in German sociology and has begun to dominate empirical research on social structure. More and more scientists put forward the idea of abandoning the traditional concept of class as well as the analysis of stratification and of replacing it by the concept of lifestyle. The present article attempts a critical evaluation of the strengths and weaknesses of this concept with regard to the following questions: (i) Which stimulations and which problems have been connected with the new paradigm? (ii) Does it measure up to its claim to be able to replace the traditional paradigm of class analysis? (iii) Is it an apt instrument for comprehending the forms of social inequality in modem societies? Those questions are answered in three steps. First, some positive new impulses are pointed out which the concept of lifestyle has given to research on social structure. Second, a number of shortcomings of this concept are discussed, which will make clear the problematic character of a sociology of lifestyles. Finally, some remarks are made on what the author regards as an adequate reconceptualization of stratification research.

AB Since the mid-80's economic sociology has experienced an enormous upturn. In this context, the notion of "social embeddedness" of economic actions as the organizing principle of economic sociology has been of particular importance. Ironically, the basic intuition that markets are socially embedded has-although containing an important insight-led economic sociologists to take the market itself for granted. In this context the paper intends to show the contribution of Pierre Bourdieu's capital theory to the explanation of the logic of market-entry processes and the way markets work.

TI The enforced europeanization of national trade unions
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID EUROPE
AB After the introduction of the European monetary union, any kind of national wage policy has become part of a supranational context. In the present paper, this process is conceptualized as the enforced Europeanization of national trade union policy. A distinctive feature of the post-Maastricht process has been the intensification of cross-border cooperations among national trade unions. This is exemplified by the so called "Doorn Declaration" and the Baltic Sea cooperation. These examples show that the different systems of collective bargaining are to a considerable degree unknown to actors across national borders, but that this institutional strangeness is gradually being overcome and a process of confidence-building is established. As a consequence, the transnational competence of trade union actors is strengthened and the Europeanization of national trade union policy is accelerated, which can be seen as the actual significance of those cooperation initiatives. That process of national trade unions catching up with Europeanization does not only lead to a shift of national politics to Europe (as neo-functionalist theory makes us believe), but rather to an internalization of Europe into national politics.

TI The perception of "benefit fraud" and the acceptance of benefits for
   unemployed people
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID WELFARE
AB Social benefits for the unemployed constitute an important institution of the German welfare state. For the years to come, an increasing or at least unchanging part of the economically active population can be expected to depend upon such programmes ("Arbeitslosengeld", "Arbeitslosenhilfe", "Hilfe zum Lebensunterhalt"), especially in the new states, i.e. the former GDR. TI Gabriel Tarde and the end of the social
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Gabriel Tarde was, together with Emile Durkheim, the founder of French sociology. He has, however, almost completely disappeared from mainstream sociology as an actually used theoretical resource, and his appearance is usually limited to historical footnotes. The re-publication of his work in French, however, has allowed a profound reappraisal of his importance. The paper tries to briefly outline some of the reasons why his work can become central to a sociology which is not obsessed-as Durkheim's was-with the social. The attention paid to networks and their significance, the importance of the sociology of science and technology, the disregard for the nature/culture-divide, the fusion of psychology and sociology, the absence of any break with philosophy and especially with metaphysics: all those features made it impossible, a century ago, to acknowledge Tarde as a genuine professional sociologist; but those same features make him one of the most exciting sociologists of today.

RP Latour, B (corresponding author), ENS Mines, Ctr Sociol Innovat, 62 Blvd St Michel, F-75006 Paris, France.

TI The traps of organisational history. On the paradoxes of the
   decentralized enterprise
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Research on organisational decentralization in sociology, psychology and business economics has mainly focussed on the unintended side-effects of decentralized organisational. structures. However, the process of re-organisation from a centralized, strongly hierarchical to a decentralized enterprise has hardly been studied. The present article demonstrates three contradictions which regularly arise in the process of transition from a centralized to a decentralized organisation. They can be referred to as the paradox of "be independent!", the paradox of "take your own decision, but with a caveat", and the paradox of "organize yourself, but not the way you used to". Bearing in mind those three paradoxes, the author suggests that the often noticed inconsistencies in the process of transition to a decentralized organisation cannot be blamed on mistakes by the management or their counsellors, but are rooted in structural and hence unresolvable contradictions.

TI Cultural diversity in organisations: Making a blind spot see
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Review
ID RELATIONAL DEMOGRAPHY; CONFLICT; CATEGORIZATION; PERFORMANCE;
   MANAGEMENT; IDENTITY
AB The article sheds light on a new and increasingly important issue for organisational research in Germany: the issue of cultural diversity in organizations. The focus of the article is workforce heterogeneity in terms of gender, nation, occupation and profession. As compared to North America, cultural diversity is a fairly new topic in Germany. We analyse whether and how the debate can be transferred to the situation in Germany and which aspects may become relevant for German organisations in the future. After clarifying conceptional issues we propose a dynamic concept of diversity and deduct pertinent cultural categories for German organisations (demographic, occupational and organisational. variables). TI Hybridization of the German system of industrial relations -
   Continuities and discontinuities within a process of radical change
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Review
AB Recent changes in the German economy have affected the company-based organisation of work, the links between intra- and inter-company levels of representation of the workforce, the institutionalisation of collective actors, and the embeddedness of industrial relations in the national context. The present paper analyses those changes in the system of collective bargaining as a dialectic simultaneity of continuities and discontinuities. The crucial point in understanding the actual logic of transition can be found in the shift from the industrial sector to the (tertiary) services sector. In those sectors-and especially in the extremely dynamic, volatile and often short-lived firms of the so-called "new economy"-the general decline of works council coverage in the whole economy coincides with the traditionally low coverage and absence of collective agreements in that sector. At the same time, white collar workers in those sectors are creating new forms of (individually based) representation of their interests, empowering new actors and establishing new bargaining models. On the whole, we face a hybridization of the German system of industrial relations.

TI Globalization and inequality - Issues of conceptualization and
   explanation
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA English
DT Article
ID COUNTRIES; INCOME
AB The conceptual part of the paper specifies the term "globalization" by distinguishing three kinds of global processes: (i) the moulding of actors and their conditions by their past. i.e., the enduring weight of global history. (ii) global flows of goods and services, of capital, of people, of information and ideas, and (iii) global entanglements of national and global institutions and organisations. Together with national processes this set of processes makes up an explanatory model of global outcomes of inequality. Inequality is also specified into three kinds: vital inequality, existential inequality. and resource inequality and four basic mechanisms of inequality are identified: distanciation, exclusion, super-/subordination and exploitation. The explanatory model is then applied to long-term developments of vital and economic inequality in the world. The former. as measured by infant mortality and life expectancy, has decreased substantially in the second half of 20th century, whereas income inequality has increased. Global flows of medical knowledge seem to have played a crucial role in reducing vital inequality. The weight of global history, as measured by GDP per capita in 1820 and 1900, and national processes of political economy appear to account for most of today's global resource inequality.

RP Therborn, G (corresponding author), Swedish Collegium Adv Study Social Sci, Gotavagen 4, S-75236 Uppsala, Sweden.

TI Expert knowledge and interaction. The theory-generating expert interview
   as a research instrument
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The expert interview is a rarely considered method in sociological research. In light of this background we discuss the complex assumptions based on the sociology of knowledge and on interaction theory that lead to a methodological consolidation of qualitative expert interviews. First. based on our general distinction between three types of expert interviews, we outline the specific features of the expert inter-view as an instrument for generating theory. In the second part we give an overview of the current debate within the sociology of knowledge on the concept of the expert and we introduce a definition of the expert that is closely related to the empirical practice. Finally we discuss the implications of such a concept of expert knowledge as an "analytical construction" for interpreting the process of interaction. Guided by the assumption that data is a product of specific interaction rather than a representation of a reality that has become independent of the continual (re)construction of meaning, we argue for a shift from an "archaeological" towards an "interactionist" model of data production. We suggest that due to the many equivalent ways of stimulating the production of expert knowledge the problem of validity as a central aspect of the expert inter-view has to be redefined.

TI Police routine and habitus: A social-ecological study
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID WORK
AB The article reports an ethnographic case study examining the adaptive reactions of policemen to an emerging "street corner society" in a Duisburg city district. The study was conducted in a poor district characterized by an ethnic polarisation between local residents and their Turkish neighbours. First, the article explains that policemen operating in arenas of the local public usually conduct most of their work applying a corporate police habitus by which they symbolically produce and reproduce their power. The use of this habitus accounts for a great part of policemen's everyday practice, such as handling civil actors and preventing the escalation of conflicts during police intervention. However, the use of a corporate police habitus also serves as a basis for policemen's adaptation to multiple social contexts in the city. Thus, in order to cope with the particular context of the "street corner society" in the above mentioned district, policemen act out an extreme machismo habitus and get involved in machismo-oriented character contests. Corporate police then turn into "street corner police". The style of performance of street corner police is based upon a concept of "honour" related to the martial ideal of chivalry, and the common ground constituted by the shared concept of honour facilitates the informal social work carried out by the police. The strategic use of character contests enables street corner police to control street corner actors, to channel social conflicts, and to even render them integrative.

TI Rituals among rockers and bikers
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB In modern society ritual is looked upon in very different ways. On the one hand rituals are regarded as anachronistic relies and forms without substance, while on the other hand social actors permanently "invent" new ritual practices. The latter fact indicates that ritual has an important social function for the constitution of everyday life. Based on Alfred Schutz' a concept of Life-World, the article argues that rituals help actors to create everyday life, which includes both acting in individual situations and generalizing from different situations. Furthermore, the article argues that the effects of rituals may be either preventive or corrective in character. All those functions of ritual are empirically verified in a study of particular subcultural communities: the communities of rockers and bikers. These communities can be characterized by three elements: a cult-like relation to motorcycles, a distinctive lifestyle expressed by clothing and habitus, and a characteristic view of the world and of man ("biker-philosophy"). Rituals among rockers and bikers, for example distinctive forms of greeting or initiation created by procedures of bricolage, are closely related to their lifestyle and thereby ensure the reproduction and handing down of their everyday life.

TI Health services for children in Germany, Austria, Great Britain, and
   Denmark
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Children depend on institutions for their protection. An important institution for the promotion of children's well-being is the health care system. The article compares different forms of health care systems and finds that in countries where children are directly insured on the basis of citizenship children's needs are addressed both more comprehensively and more specifically than in countries where children's rights to protection are derived from their status as dependants of an insured family member. This is empirically tested by comparing Great Britain and Denmark on the one hand (national health service) and Germany and Austria on the other (compulsory health insurance). Great Britain and Denmark offer comprehensive health care and prevention for children up to the end of compulsory schooling. Health programmes are directed and co-ordinated by a single institution. Go-operation between the various providers ensures that a significant part of the child population - particularly at-risk groups - undergo health examinations. By contrast, in Germany and Austria the individual's responsibility for his or her own health is emphasised and it is left up to parents to take advantage of the recommended early intervention programmes. These systems encourage competition between providers, which makes it more difficult to co-ordinate health services for children. A comparison between Germany and Austria shows, however, that it is not necessary to change from one system to the other in order to better address children's needs, but that reforms within the existing system may do.
RP Wendt, C (corresponding author), Bahnhofstr 23, D-69115 Heidelberg, Germany.

TI Tocqueville and Weber on the sociological origins of citizenship: The
   political culture of American democracy
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB While Alexis de Tocqueville's commentary on American democracy is famous, Max Weber's is far less so. However, in scattered writings, Weber addresses two of the themes at the centre of Tocqueville's analysis of the American political culture's "manners and mores": the potential for a "tyranny of the majority" in the US and the critical role of civil associations. By reference to these two themes, this study seeks to examine the divergent perspectives of these classical theorists on the political culture of the US, contrast Tocqueville's more structural and interest-based mode of analysis to Weber's emphasis upon the significance of values and beliefs, and comment upon, in light of the insights offered by both theorists, the sociological origins of citizenship. Unlike Tocqueville, Weber sees an odd juxtaposition-an accentuated, "world mastery" individualism and an accentuated orientation to civic sphere ideals-at the centre of the American political culture.

TI Women between tradition and modernity. Traditional gender relations in a
   modern society: Korea
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB In Korea, gender relations are characterized by a specific combination of tradition and modernity. They can be seen as an aspect of the process of modernization. The Confucian family structure - familism and the man-centred family system - serves as a cultural framework for gender relations. Although the sphere of family, marriage and women has considerably changed during the process of modernization, it has not led to a fundamental change in traditional gender relations. Due to a specific combination of traditional Confucian cultural ideals on the one hand and modern capitalist-industrial economy on the other, the process of marriage contributes to the reproduction and stabilization of traditional gender relations. Empirical research on everyday family life after marriage clearly demonstrates that while many women accept conflicts with traditional values and norms, others submit to tradition. Generally, Korean family life is centred around the husband and his family. Even families living in Germany who can escape from the direct influence and interference by the husband's parent family do not practise modern gender roles and a modern division of labour. In Korea, a conflict between the mother-in-law and the daughter-in-law can frequently be observed, which is a manifestation of the generation gap modified by the typical Korean family structure. The article concludes by asking what would be required for the establishment of modern gender relations in Korea and finds: first, the establishment of various social spheres and groups, second, the improvement of social policies, and third, an increased individualism, which could be achieved by changing patterns of school education.
RP Kim, DY (corresponding author), Jugong Apt 69-401,Chamshil 1 Dong,Songpa Ku, Seoul 138221, South Korea.

TI The social acceptance of the welfare state. A review of literature and a
   new perspective
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID PUBLIC-OPINION; CLASS-POLITICS; UNITED-STATES; ATTITUDES; FINLAND;
   POLLS; CONSENSUS; SECURITY; SUPPORT; POLICY
AB For a long time the social acceptance and public support of the welfare state has been a major concern in theoretical debates and empirical research. This article reviews empirical research on the public support of the welfare state. The results of national and comparative research have corroborated an overwhelmingly high and stable support for the key institutions of the welfare state. However, some of the findings are quite contradictory while others are questionable from a methodological point of view. For example, it remains an unanswered question how the continuously high level of public support of the welfare state can be explained. Moreover, it is doubtful whether there is really such a high degree of public acceptance. In particular, the various ways in which the dependent (acceptance) and independent variables (self-interest, value orientations) are operationalised is open to challenge. This article shows how some of these deficiencies can be overcome.

TI Variants of constructivism in the sociology of social problems
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID CONSEQUENCES
AB Within the recent Sociology of Social Problems (SSP) in North America three main variants of constructionism have emerged: a reflexive, a strict and a contextual one. PT J
AU Holtgrewe, U
AF Holtgrewe, U
TI "Whoever has got the problem has got the solution as well." -
   Structuration and Pragmatist Theory of Agency Applied to Organisational
   Change
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID INNOVATION
AB The paper tries to specify the theory of structuration with the aim of applying it to acting in organisations. "Reorganisation" changes the interrelationship between the routinised reproduction and the transformation of organisational structures. Routines are open to challenge and reference to routine loses its legitimacy. "More" innovativity is demanded on all organisational levels.
   These changes in empirical organisations require a theoretical approach to take a closer look at agency along the lines of routine, creativity and innovation and to explore the interplay of past, present and future in the action. However, as the theory of structuration suggests, action recursively draws on structure, along the dimensions of domination over rules and resources, signification and legitimation. Thus the structurationist model of organisation is expanded by recent neo-pragmatist arguments. These theoretical considerations are examined by drawing on two empirical case studies conducted at Deutsche Telekom AG which implemented measures of reorganisation concerning market orientation and flexibilisation of personnel. It shows that on the local level the organisational past retains its importance both as a constraint and as a resource. Creative action articulates organisational past, present and future along the dimensions of domination, signification and legitimation - both in accordance with and against the market and future orientation of reorganisation.
C1 Gerhard Mercator Univ Duisburg, FB 1, Fach Soziol, D-47048 Duisburg, Germany.
RP Holtgrewe, U (corresponding author), Gerhard Mercator Univ Duisburg, FB 1, Fach Soziol, D-47048 Duisburg, Germany.

PT J
AU Canzler, W
AF Canzler, W
TI The car in your imagination and outside your house: The interrelation
   between individualization and use of the car
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB Based on empirical research on a new and highly innovative car sharing-project the article claims that in German society individuals' lifestyles and the availability of automobiles are linked in a self-reinforcing feedback process. Data gathered from first round panel interviews focusing on patterns of mobility and activities show that particular means of transport encourage particular lifestyles and vice versa. Moreover, the characteristics of patterns of mobility touch on categories fundamental to social sciences, such as household and family, as well as on categories central to transport research, such as choice of routes and time budgets. A first look at these categories shows a confusing picture well-known from other studies. There is a wide variety of biographies, of organisation of work, housekeeping and leisure time. There is neither a clear pattern nor a predominant model in the variety of lifestyles. However, the results of the interviews show that the use of means of transport is widely integrated into daily life and has become a routine to all persons interviewed. These findings are not only relevant to social science research on transport and mobility, but have also consequences for some basic categories for the analysis of social reality.
C1 WZB, D-10785 Berlin, Germany.
RP Canzler, W (corresponding author), WZB, Reichpietschufer 50, D-10785 Berlin, Germany.

PT J
AU Burkart, G
AF Burkart, G
TI Mobile communication. The cultural significance of the "handy"
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID INTEGRATION; TELEPHONE
AB Within the past few years the mobile phone -in Germany called "handy" - has been an overwhelming success. The main interest concerning the "handy" is nor in its properties as a technological device, but in it as an artefact that - pars pro tote - represents some aspects of fundamental cultural change. By making it possible to reach anybody at any time, the mobile phone not only facilitates communication with distant people or people who are involved in some outdoor activity - on the beach, on a mountain, in the desert -, it also shifts the boundaries between the private and the public spheres, between personal and professional communication. The mobile phone is an object of material culture that combines three basic elements of modem societies: communication, mobility, and individuality. It is an artefact which incorporates social practices and cultural knowledge, a "prosthetic" object merging body and culture. The cultural implementation of the mobile phone raises a number of questions concerning culture and communication. This paper focuses on two problems. First: How does the mobile phone enhance options of communication, and what are the specific problems resulting from it? And second: What communicative problems arise due to the interference of mobile communication with face-fo-face-communication in public space, and what new rules of public communication are institutionalised by discursive and practical negotiations?.
C1 Univ Luneburg, Inst Sozialwissensch, D-21332 Luneburg, Germany.
RP Burkart, G (corresponding author), Univ Luneburg, Inst Sozialwissensch, D-21332 Luneburg, Germany.

PT J
AU Keller, R
AF Keller, R
TI Waste in the public sphere. Reflexive modernization as cultural
   transformation - A comparison of France and Germany
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The paper examines to which degree the occupational structure in the German civil service is affected by principles proposed in a comprehensive administrative reform put forward in the 1990s. It considers the consequences of the proposed reform model for the existing Affirmative Action policy implemented in the civil service, it argues that by modifying certain contractual norms in order to enhance the responsiveness to the goals of the organisation, the reform model affects those components of the civil service's occupational structure that have a gender dimension. Those components have been derived from the underlying principles of a type of occupation-the civil servant-which came into being in the course of the institutionalization of modern bureaucracy in the German stares of the 19th century and, moreover, in the context of the differentiation of work and family as well as the establishment of a gender division of labour within the family. Furthermore, the relationship between the reform model and the Affirmative Action policy introduced during the 1980s and ' 90s is discussed. This policy was based on a new legal understanding of equal rights which no longer considered equality of opportunities to be guaranteed if individual abilities were equal. The reasoning underlying this approach, by which the legal foundations for a new type of equal opportunity policy were established, is contrasted with the reasoning underlying the administrative reform concepts outlined above. Finally, the paper assesses the chances of success of the new equal opportunity policy that is part of the planned administrative reform model.
C1 Univ Augsburg, Wirtschafts & Sozialwissensch Fak, D-86135 Augsburg, Germany.
RP Keller, R (corresponding author), Univ Augsburg, Wirtschafts & Sozialwissensch Fak, D-86135 Augsburg, Germany.

PT J
AU Ozcan, V
   Seifert, W
AF Ozcan, V
   Seifert, W
TI Self-employment of immigrants in Germany: Exclusion or path to
   integration?
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID ENTREPRENEURSHIP
AB In Germany, as in several other European countries, the number of self-employed immigrants has steadily increased throughout the past years, which might be interpreted as an indicator of the increasing integration of immigrants into German society. However, it has been argued that this development has been caused by the rising level of unemployment among foreigners and that for this reason the forced self-employment will not contribute to the social and economic integration of former guest-workers. On the contrary-so the argument goes-, the marginal position of the self-employed will rather resemble those of wage-earners.
   By analysing the German Microcensus of 1995 we tried to find out whether the self-employment of immigrants in Germany could be interpreted as a sign of integration. For this purpose, we compared Germans with the foreign population, which we divided into two groups: immigrants from countries most former guest-workers came from, such as Greece and Turkey, were distinguished from immigrants from industrial nations, such as the United States, France, Great Britain, and others. It is well known that these two groups differ considerably in their socio-economic characteristics. Therefore, the starting positions for self-employment show significant differences for the two groups.
   Our findings confirm that the self-employment of immigrants from former guest-worker countries does not have the same quality in terms of branches and income as the self-employment of Germans and foreigners from industrial nations. At the same time, however, it turns out that among immigrants from former guest-worker countries the self-employed have higher levels of education and income than workers and employees. A logistic regression confirms the more favourable income structure of the self-employed while controlling for relevant variables. For this reason, the increasing number of self-employed immigrants from former guest-worker countries can certainly be considered as a sign of their gradual integration.
C1 Humboldt Univ, D-10099 Berlin, Germany.
RP Ozcan, V (corresponding author), Humboldt Univ, Unter Linden 6, D-10099 Berlin, Germany.
EM veysel.oezcan@rz.hu-berlin.de

TI "I am just a Jew and then a Russian". The process of acculturation of
   young Russian Jews in the course of time
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The article examines the question whether the naturalization of migrants is an indicator of their adaptation to and identification with the receiving society. A longitudinal study of young Russian Jews who migrated to Berlin in 1989/90 and who were interviewed in 1995/96 and in 1998/99 inquires whether those who have been naturalized are more inclined to have social relations with Germans and to stay in Germany than those who hesitate to be naturalized or reject naturalization altogether. Results suggest that naturalization has no positive effect on the process of acculturation. However, there is some evidence that citizenship is not only acquired for instrumental reasons but is in itself appreciated as the starting-point of political participation.

   PRAXIS

DT Article
ID ORGANIZATION THEORY; MYTH
AB The theory of new institutionalism has become a prominent approach in organizational analysis. PT J
AU Schafer, M
AF Schafer, M
TI Globalization as domination. A critical comment on John W. Meyer's
   macro-sociological institutional theory
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID WORLD
AB Globalization, understood as the world-wide spread of western institutions and particularly of the modem form of organisation, is the focus of the macro-sociological institutional theory developed at Stanford University by John W. Meyer et al. Having become popular in organisational studies in the 1980s, this approach concentrates on the increasing isomorphism in both the structure of social practices and the construction of social entities in accordance with "western cultural accounts". Researchers point out the amazing homogeneity in models available for the construction and regulation of social life. Social patterns that differ from dominant western institutions do not gain significance on world level.
   The article argues that although the approach by Meyer et al. is reasonably able to analyse homogenization, it lacks the theoretical means to explain asymmetry, i.e. the trend towards inequality on a world-wide level. This asymmetry in the structure of "world society" is the focus of Immanuel Wallerstein's world-system theory. The author suggests that a synthesis of these two macro-sociological theories will allow to define globalization as domination, understood as a combination of both institutional homogenization and structural asymmetry. From an emancipatory perspective, the author suggests to discuss ways to induce some global dynamics of de-institutionalization.
RP Schafer, M (corresponding author), Paulussenstr 12, D-42349 Wuppertal, Germany.

TI Inequality, exclusion and justice
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 30th Congress of the Deutschen-Gesellschaft-for-Sociology
CY SEP 26-29, 2000
CL COLOGNE, GERMANY
SP Deutsch Gesell Sociol
ID EQUALITY; INJUSTICE
AB The article deals with the normative foundations underlying (or needed by) sociological research on inequality. Since sociology as a positive discipline is incapable of providing such foundations itself, it needs to borrow them elsewhere, especially-as is maintained here-from political theory and welfare economics. Combining important elements drawn from sociological differentiation theory with (portions of) the works of John Rawls and Michael Walzer, an outline of a conception of justice is drawn which promises to lay the necessary groundwork and hence to serve as a basis for guiding normatively relevant empirical research.

TI Institutional contexts of technological innovations: The debate on
   genetic engineering in Germany and the USA
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The article uses the example of the debate on genetic engineering in Germany and the USA to discuss the interrelation between institutional order, societal conflict settlement, and the political implementation of new technologies, The configuration of the institutional arrangement, which is the frame in which the settlement of conflicts takes place, is modeled in terms of center and periphery. It is argued that a dynamic relationship between center and periphery granting equal chances of access to the arena of conflict to all parties is more likely to produce some viable consensus among the actors involved than the institutionalized separation between center and periphery, which tends to create much more rigid and uncompromising positions. From such institutional configurations conclusions may be drawn as to the innovative behavior of a society.

   Central Europe
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS

DT Article
AB The paper analyses the process of the granting of loans in the lending business. AU Strulik, T

TI The functions and consequences of private rating agencies in the context
   of the regulation of global financial markets
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The increasing importance of rating agencies as organizations specialized on credit evaluation demonstrates that a global financial economy also produces globally oriented organizations which reflexively contribute to the concentration of financial decisions. Furthermore, the use of such ratings in contexts of legal control seems to emphasize the significance of mixed public-private forms of regulation which make use of market actors' expertise and intimate knowledge of problems. Shedding light on both aspects, the article examines the role of rating agencies in the regulation of global financial markets. Using concepts developed in risk sociology and sociology of knowledge it shows that, on the one hand, rating agencies indeed contribute to the handling of economic risks by constructing virtual worlds which stabilize expectations, while, on the other hand, in fulfilling their manifest function, they also produce new contingencies and uncertainties. Rating agencies improve the capacity for managing complexity of the self-referentially operating financial markets; but that is the very reason why they follow the logic of a functionally differentiated society tending towards an increase in options and contribute to the further growth of ignorance and the riskiness of financial markets. As to "regulation by rating" it is obvious that while the use of ratings expands the internal complexity of the regulatory regime, it inevitably produces new problems as well.
C1 Univ Bielefeld, Fak Soziol, D-33615 Bielefeld, Germany.
RP Strulik, T (corresponding author), Univ Bielefeld, Fak Soziol, Univ Str 25, D-33615 Bielefeld, Germany.

TI Money-crisis-generation. Socio-monetary journeys through the 20th
   century
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
AB The article presents first results of an empirical study on the transformation of behaviour as to money and on the social effects of the major currency events in 20th century Germany. The particular approach in the design of this study is that the total of 144 individuals interviewed included people from three generations within each single family. Whereas the causes of inflation have been the object of inquiry in many scientific studies, the effects of inflation regarding social character, socio-economic, cultural, and gender-specific aspects have largely escaped the scope of sociological research. This study shows the longevity of monetary norms, behaviour, and dispositions over the course of a century. Even projections into the future regarding monetary processes are often formed along the lines of models of the past and interpreted according to corresponding cognitive patterns, It shows that, when faced with a frightening economic crisis, only an informed minority of people behave according to textbook expectations. Adaptation of behaviour takes place only with considerable time lags over generations.
C1 Univ Gottingen, Soziol Seminar, D-37073 Gottingen, Germany.

AU Preisendorfer, P
AF Preisendorfer, P
TI Structural and situational factors as determinants of the choice of
   means of transport
SO SOZIALE WELT-ZEITSCHRIFT FUR SOZIALWISSENSCHAFTLICHE FORSCHUNG UND
   PRAXIS
LA German
DT Article
ID PLANNED BEHAVIOR; EMPIRICAL-TEST; ATTITUDES; CAR
AB Within the research on individual choices of means of transport two approaches compete with each other: behavioural models and attitudinal models. In spite of a dominance of attitudinal models in current research, the present paper favours behavioural models. Based on a survey in Restock (Germany), the article demonstrates that the choice of means of transport for different purposes (work, shopping, leisure) can be sufficiently explained by a small number of structural and situational factors and that-as compared to that-general attitudes play a minor role. The two structural factors that are shown to be most important are, on the one hand, the availability of a car and, on the other hand, the difference in time needed to get from here to there by car and by public transport respectively. The minor significance of attitudes is demonstrated by examining the effects of-general and traffic-specific-environmental awareness.
